< Text>
I have been craving Lumpia since the place in my town shut down years ago. Friends make it for me here and there but I can never get it when I want it. As kid at one of my friends birthday parties she would also serve Lumpia. It was so good and I've loved it ever since.
I searched for local spots that served Lumpia. Lots came up but only a few in my "backyard ". So we made the drive. The location was easy to find. Parking was easy too. Due to current circumstances they are only serving takeout which was fine for me. The staff was very friendly and helpful with ordering food. The menu has lots of items to choose from.
I came for Lumpia only this trip and it did not dissapoint. I was so elated. I ordered two orders of the pork Lumpia and it was not enough. The Lumpia was cooked just to my liking and the sauce to go with it was a perfect match. When all the Lumpia was gone I was so bummed. Obviously I'm going back it's just a matter of when. Probably sooner than later. I introduced them to my son as well and it was a hit for him</Text>

<userid>112996515509724275655< /userid><user_name>Nathaniel Maghanoy<//user_name><Date>1566352830142</Date><Rating>5<//Rating>< Review>
DELICIOUS!

Growing up in a very large Filipino family, I came in with high expectations and was not let down. On my first(and second) visit I had the pork sisig which they topped with a fried egg and served on a bed of rice and banana leaf. Rich and savory seasoning that brought back some childhood memories. My friend, a white girl whose never had Filipino food beyond Lumpia, had the egg noodle pancit and halo halo; she loved both.

My third visit I had the Lechon(crispy pork belly, pictured). A perfect crispy crust sealed in succulent fatty pork belly.

The restaurant is extremely clean with a contemporary aesthetic and flourishes of Filipino cultural artifacts. Customer service, by whom I assume to be the owners, was excellent every time. I highly recommend for anyone looking to try Filipino cuisine or something different.<//Review>

<userid>117904783283459124409< /userid><name>Rodney<//name><Date>1517690675479< /Date>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< Text>
Templeton Park is a great park for a kids play day or other get together event.

There's a large grilling and seating area with great summer shade. The park itself also has large trees throughout offing lots of large shady spots.

The weekly year round famers market held on Saturday 9am-12 is amongst the best in the country.

They also host a concert in the park series in the summer along with numerous other events year round.

For the water types you also have the summing pool. Which adds a great extra activity for family events held in the park.</Text>

< Text>
Nice size park.  Decent playground and a lot of open grass areas and several nice tables with bbqs by some. Larger bbq for events. Fairly decent gazebo in center of park. Water fountains and bathrooms as well. Beautiful trees but with younger kids it's worth mentioning that there's not much in the way of fencing or borders from surrounding active streets.  And ants and wasps can be an issue in some parts of the year at this park. Great central location though also near highway,  food,  and gas. Templeton is beautiful if you've never seen it you ought to.</Text>

<rate>5< /rate><Text>This is one of the best brunch establishments I've ever been to, and I'll definitely be back! Their fusion approach to breakfast/lunch foods is to die for.

If you're looking for basic breakfast fare, try the breakfast combo -- you'll get a plate piled high with crispy, buttery potatoes, homemade sausage, eggs cooked to perfection, and thick cut buttered toast to boot.

And if you're looking for something not so basic? Well, you have the rest of the menu! Try their iced linguine -- cold noodles in a tomato dashi broth with crisp cucumbers, thin sliced pickled radish, and perfectly grilled sweet corn with a poached egg nestled on top. It's summer in a bowl! And please, don't sleep on their drinks. Their nitro cold brew is delicious, and their yuzu sparkling lemonade is to die for.

The service is impeccable as well, especially with COVID protocols...they are careful to keep folks distanced, and even more careful to clean between parties. Check them out if you haven't already -- they've made a regular out of me! :)< /Text><pictures>None<//pictures>< response>

< review>
Steps to order - no waiters or table service: 1) grab a pencil and menu, 2) fill out what you want to order by looking at the laminated pictures and marking your choice of food, 3) walk up to the register with your menu and selected items, 4) pay and seat yourself anywhere in the restaurant. Don't forget to grab yourself napkins, utensil, and water after getting your seat. Great idea on restaurant concept. I came during lunch hour so food came out slow and there were 3 chefs in the kitchen in a packed house, every seat was filled. I ordered a peppered fried chicken sandwich and it was DELICIOUS. Fresh ingredients and very juicy and flavorful. Clean food and enough to last me through the office without food coma since I did not order any sides. Recommend but plan on waiting a bit during rush. Parking was tight, you might have to park in street or the plaza next door before walking over. I would come back again for brunch items though, those look amazing.< /review>

<user_id>107590505454040594006<//user_id><name>Ashtar Bilip< /name>< Time>
1559935870051</Time>
< rate>
5</rate>
< review>
Came here this weekend while I was in the area. This place is very unassuming from the outside but the vibe inside is super warm and relaxed.

When you arrive, you mark off your order on a form and bring it to the register when you're ready to order. They give you a number after you pay and you find a table. They mark off your ticket as they bring out your items.

This time I tried the fried chicken bun, pork bun, fried cabbage salad, potatoes bravas and the blood orange hibiscus agua fresca. Everything was so good! The buns they use to make the sandwiches are soft but not too soft to get soggy. The pork was tender and had some melty cheese, onions and a sauce that tied it all together perfectly. The fried chicken sandwich was good too, but I think I liked the pork more. The chicken was moist and well seasoned and the pickles were fresh and crisp. They put a honey mustard sauce on it that was a bit overwhelming to me but overall super good.

The sides were standout to me. The cabbage salad was fresh and crisp; it had a slightly sweet sesame dressing and had avo, tomato and cucumber in it - so good! The potatoes bravas were a nice hat tip to Spanish tapas - they were moist and flavorful and I loved the fried egg on top.

The agua fresca was just the right level of sweet and was super refreshing. Truly, this is a place where I imagine everything on the menu is stellar. Would definitely come back if I was in the neighborhood and want to try some other menu items!!<//review>

< Text>
Painter's Tape is an excellent new breakfast/lunch spot in the South Bay!    I have been there multiple times in the short time that they have been open!  The decor is so cute.  The painter's theme runs through the restaurant - from the custom lighting to the spice jar labels, blue accents on the chairs - even the labeling on to-go orders!   My favorites so far are the Pepper Fried Chicken Bun, the Texas Toast, Breakfast Salad, and the Summer Fruit with Greek Yogurt.  Make sure to try the agua fresca!  It was Strawberry Lychee on Sunday!

One thing to note - the ordering method is a little different.  There are menus and checklists on a table when you walk in the door.  You take a checklist and mark off the items you would like to order and take that to the cashier.  They hand you a table marker and your drinks and then you seat yourself.  Food is brought out to your table as soon it's made - by the chefs themselves!  Pretty cool!

I've noticed that the ramen place next door is closed on Wednesdays, leaving the parking open for Painter's Tape customers!< /Text>

<review>Stopped by for a quick lunch nearby. Painter's Tape was opened by a former MB Post sous chef, which I love going to. The menu is japanese inspired breakfast/lunch cafe food. The restaurant itself is not too big with some tables, regular for groups of four or high standing ones. You first order with the menu pamplet sheets and dry erase markers like at a dim sum place and bring it to the cashier to pay.

I got a yuzu lemonade, which was very refreshing with the perfect sweetness, to drink. And also ordered a shabu shabu burger, which was basically a roast beef sando with kewpie mayo, a katsu BBQ style sauce, and lettuce that came with honey coated potato chips plus a curry cheese donut. The donut was great, with the flavorful curry cheese filling shining through but could've used a bit more to fill the airpocket. Sando was nice but the roast beef was maybe a tad too dry and thinly cut. I really liked the honey potato chips. The coating is very glazed, but still crunchy.

Overall, a cool interesting neighborhood spot for breakfast and lunch.<//review>< response>
None</response>

<Text>OlOverall, this place was pretty cool. Even the decorations inside are awesome--they go along with the theme of the restaurant name! Small shared parking lot, though. The customer service was great!!

My brother, sister-in-law, and I ordered a lot of different things because we wanted to try it all! (And because I'm only in LA for the weekend!)

Soft Scrambled Eggs on Texas Toast:
This was decent. Could use a touch more salt--not something I would order again for $7.

Japanese Curry & Cheese Donut:
This was OK, too. Again, not something I would die/crave for.

Grilled Zucchini:
Hmm this was okay. If I didn't have anything else, I would eat the whole plate of them, but it was average.

Potatoes Brava:
I actually didn't try this, but my brother and his wife thought it was pretty good. The egg jiggles & yolk ooooozes out onto the potatoes!

Pork Toro Bun:
Basically Pork Belly on bun. This was pretty good, but I wish the pork was more tender.

Pepper Fried Chicken Bun:
This was delicious!! The chicken was very moist, juicy, & flavorful! Would definitely order again!

Shabu Steak Bun:
This one was yummy as well. My fave was the Pepper Fried Chicken Bun.

Honey Butter Chips:
Soooooooo good!! I want more! Comes with sandwich entrees!

Gem Lettuce:
This one was actually our favorite out of all the veggies. So glad I ordered this, despite the fact that the cashier recommended other items that I didn't fancy as much...over this Gem Lettuce Salad!</Text>< user>

< review>
Painter"s Tape is not your father's greasy spoon. They are only open for breakfast and lunch, but don't be fooled the food here is fresh, flavorful and made to order. Menu items are inventive with a modern spin. I had the week day breakfast special, two eggs (sunny side), potatoes, garlicy pork sausage and Texas toast. Sounds simple enough, but the eggs were cooked to perfection, the potatoes (cottage style) were crispy on the outside, soft on the inside and well seasoned, but the real stand out here was the sausage patty. Pure porky perfection with enough garlic to play well against the richness of the egg yolks popped and running into the potatoes. A perfect bite. There is no wait staff, upon entering you fill out an order form then take it to the kitchen and seat yourself. When the food is ready one of the cooks brings your order to the table. Drink selection is limited, but what they do offer is delicious agua fresca, coffee and alcoholic offerings as well. Can't wait to sample the rest of the menu.</review>

103061686482542489750< /user>
<text>Great Comfort Food!<//text></record>
</dataset><record>
< Text>
Visiting, what was the original Burnt Tortilla location, we had breakfast totally enjoying each dish.  The passion fruit water was refreshing and spot on, not to sweet or watered down.  The potatoes saltado were flavorful drawing from the Peruvian dish, Lomo saltado.  Great wake up dish!
Followed by the stewed organic rice!  This was the best dish we ordered.  Not sure, what I was expecting but I was delectable impressed.  Looking like a porridge, the rice has a slightly chewy consistent mixed with the hearty yet light chicken and tomato seasoning, made it a comforting flavorful delight.
The Texas toast, a memorable flavor which reminded me of my Dad who would describe eating a Hawaiian version of Melba toast for breakfast slathered with condensed milk.  The inch thick toast covered with the honey and condensed milk made for a simple dessert like quality for breakfast.
Ending with the yeast waffle, the delicate crispy lightness of the waffle reminded me of the Waffle design Liege truck with less heavy feeling.  It was not overly heavy typical waffle, light and airy with the sweet chocolate and banana toppings.  The walnuts give it an added crunch.
The decor was a homage and tribute to their father and his business.  He must be a proud Dad!
Great place and food.  We will be back for more!</Text>

<userid>111158142056966751770< /userid><user_name>Tiffany Duong</user_name><time>1514930880572<//time>< Rate>
5<//Rate>
<review>Believe the hype! This local hotspot is casual and simple, but beautiful. The food is like Asian fusion food made by actual Asians, so the flavor profile feels modern but still honoring traditional tastes. There are textures, colors, and beautiful plating of each dish. There's tons of restraint in the cooking, and it never feels like it is lacking or trying to hard. It hits that elusive fusion note perfectly.

My bf and I were completely impressed by this and spent half our lunch telling everyone else we knew in the south bay that they should try this spot. We ordered the $12 lunch special (any sandwich, any drink, and their butter chips). We opted for the Pork Toro burger, with seared toro pieces topped with chicharones. It was interesting and savory but not too heavy. The chips were out of this world -- sweet, salty, crunchy. Totally unexpected. I also ordered the fried cabbage salad for $8. This was both our favorite dish -- there's crispy noodles in it, and the cabbage still has a crisp despite being fried. Dressing is present but not overwhelming, and there's slight hints of citrus to freshen it all up. Finally we ordered the potatoes bravas, which were filling and good.

Parking can be elusive in their dedicated lot, but there's street parking around as well. Come and see for yourself. This place is amazing!</review><pictures>None</pictures>< Response>

<user>108982914109486066023</user><username>Matteo Capanna</username><Time>1539204342345</Time><Rate>5<//Rate><review>I needed some new tires as my 215/50R17 MXM4 Michelin tires had failed to hold air at 3/32.  I would describe the tread as flaky with moderately cracked side wall to boot after nearly 4 years of use.  Let's just say they didn't make the 55,000 mark but I did a little more dirt and gravel driving than most people expose their tires to.
Knowing that I would be doing less rural and more highway driving I want something quite, comfortable, with some honest longevity.
Having purchased many tires of different brand and quality, I put Justin at ATD through the paces finding just the right tire for my needs.  I told him what I wanted, what I didn't, and what I currently was looking at.  After narrowing down the field, we battered around impression of a few tires.  Not only was the service and price excellent, we found a solution that could be installed the same day. I appreciate them getting me out the door to pick up my kids on time from school.  Thank you so much for the great tire buying experience!
So you're probably wondering what tires I chose?  Yokohama Avid Ascend GT.  It's only been a trip to Pismo for the weekend, a little rural driving in Templeton, and a couple days of usual driving in Clovis and Fresno.  My impressions: The Yokohama hands down better traction the the Michelin ever had, I'm truly impressed with the grip on clean flat roads, sandy roads, and oddly shape dips on hilly roads.
Next they are slightly noisier than than the MXM4s, but you can only tell that with the radio off, so not a deal breaker.
Both tires are 95V rated and the handling is similar.  Putting the tires through the paces is not wise when this new, but it handled all the curvy roads in a comfortably agresive manner without my wife saying slow down, yet again impressive.
These tires act like a performance tire, but feel more like a touring tire, you may or may not appreciate that feeling, and can be a little unsettling to the agresive driver who likes the connected to the road feeling normally associated with performance touring or sport tires.
Logevitity is yet to be seen, but Yokohama has a great reputation in that department.

So did I get everything I was looking for in new tires for my 2003 Acura TL type S?  I seriously doubt there was a better choice for me and my car, especially at this price.  Let them find the right tire for your needs at the right price.  Don't forget to check for rebates.< /review>< pictures>

<text>I have been a customer of America's Tire Depot at the Shaw Ave location for over a year and a half, and have waited to write this review to see if things could improve. During my time as a customer, this store has gone through three managers and numerous employee changes in the shop. Though the personnel are nice and knoweledgable, there is still a huge disconnect and lack of organization in getting the work done. This has led to numerous appointments being made either online or by phone getting lost, or unacceptable wait times when they do remember your appointment. It took over 4hrs to get tires and an alignment with an appointment this last time, and sadly was not an isolated incident. So why do I go back?!... unfortunately, I am locked into a warranty battle. I originally purchased a set of four tires with a 45,000 mile warranty on 06-09-16. Almost a year later at only 4/32nds tread wear left  and 16,500 miles on the tires respectively, the tires were too worn for them to rotate any longer due to safety reasons, but not worn enough to warranty the tire. All rotations, alignments, and any other work suggested by ATD was done over that course of time. I continued to rotate the tires myself and bring the wear down to 2/32nds respectively and 22,000 miles. While they did eventually prorate the tires, increased fees on the same tire, labor, and the expired promotion that the original set were purchased under brought the 50% off proration total to nearly the same cost I originally paid on my first set. My advice, call around and compare estimates. While tire prices can be good here, by the time you add up warranty certificates, and shop labor, the cost of their tires overall may not be a great deal when compared to other companies that offer these services as part of the purchase. Also, with the lack of organization, long wait times, and hassle proving your warranty and infringing on your time as a customer, any cost savings, if any, are negligible.</text><GmapID>0x80945b939952358f:0x8d7bcd6444be7b62< /GmapID>< pics>
